?menudm|badpoisondamage
/em : #name is hurt by poison!
%{VALUE|template} {{name=#name Poison}} {{Damage = [[ [[ round(%{VALUE|hpmax}/16) ]] * ?{Which turn of bad poison is this?|0} ]] }}

?menudm|badpoisonstart
/em : #name is badly poisoned!

?menudm|burn
/w dm %{VALUE|template} {{name=[**x**](`#[Menu_dm]) Burn}} {{"is burned!" = [**+**](`#?menudm|burnstart)}} {{Damage = [**+**](`#?menudm|burndamage)}}

?menudm|burndamage
/em : #name is hurt by their burn!
%{VALUE|template} {{name=#name Burn}} {{Damage = [[ round(%{VALUE|hpmax}/8) ]] }}

?menudm|burnstart
/em : #name is burned!
%{VALUE|template} {{name=#name Burn}} {{Effect = -1 ATK CS}}

?menudm|capturerate
/w gm %{VALUE|template} {{name=[**x**](`#[Menu_dm]) #name Capture Rate}} {{Base Rate = [[[[0@{selected|BATK}]] + [[0@{selected|BDEF}]] +[[0@{selected|BSPEED}]] + [[0@{selected|BSPATK}]] + [[0@{selected|BSPDEF}]] + 5 * %{VALUE|level}]]}} {{Current HP = [[%{VALUE|hp}/%{VALUE|hpmax}*100]]%}} {{Modifiers = <100% HP = -10
<50% HP = -25
<25% HP = -40
-20 per status effect}}

?menudm|confusion
/w dm %{VALUE|template} {{name=[**x**](`#[Menu_dm]) Confusion}} {{Duration = [**+**](`#?menudm|confusionduration)}} {{"is confused!" = [**+**](`#?menudm|confusionstart)}} {{"do they?" = [**+**](`#?menudm|confusionsave)}} {{"they do!" = [**+**](`#?menudm|confusiondamage)}} {{"is no longer!" = [**+**](`#?menudm|confusionend)}}

?menudm|confusiondamage
/em : #name hurts themself in their confusion!
%{VALUE|template} {{name=#name Confusion}} {{Damage = [[ { 2d8 + #attack + #stab|NORMAL - #defense|target1 , #minimumdamage|target1 }kh1 * #effect|NORMAL|target1 ]]}}

?menudm|confusionduration
/w dm %{VALUE|template} {{name=[**x**](`#[Menu_dm]) #name Confusion}} {{Duration = [[1d4]] turn(s)}}

?menudm|confusionend
/em : #name is no longer confused!

?menudm|confusionsave
/em : #name is confused! Do they hurt themself?
%{VALUE|template} {{name=#name Confusion}} {{Save = [[d2]]}}

?menudm|curse
/w dm %{VALUE|template} {{name=[**x**](`#[Menu_dm]) Curse}} {{"is cursed!" = [**+**](`#?menudm|cursestart)}} {{Damage = [**+**](`#?menudm|cursedamage)}}

?menudm|cursedamage
/em : #name is hurt by the curse!
%{VALUE|template} {{name=#name Curse}} {{Damage = [[ round(%{VALUE|hpmax}/4) ]] }}

?menudm|cursestart
/em : #name is cursed!

?menudm|confusionstart
/em : #name is confused!

?menudm|endofbattle
/em : End Battle! All temporary stat changes are reset!
/w dm %{VALUE|template} {{name=Stat Change Reset}} {{Check = [**+**](`#?menudm|statchangereset)}}

?menudm|flinch
/em : #name flinches!

?menudm|freeze
/w dm %{VALUE|template} {{name=[**x**](`#[Menu_dm]) Freeze}} {{"is frozen!" = [**+**](`#?menudm|freezestart)}} {{"do they thaw?" = [**+**](`#?menudm|freezesave)}} {{"is no longer!" = [**+**](`#?menudm|freezeend)}}

?menudm|freezeend
/em : #name is no longer frozen!

?menudm|freezesave
/em : #name is frozen! Do they thaw?
%{VALUE|template} {{name=#name Freeze}} {{Save = [[ d5cf<4cs=5 ]]}}

?menudm|freezestart
/em : #name is frozen!

?menudm|infatuation
/w dm %{VALUE|template} {{name=[**x**](`#[Menu_dm]) Infatuation}} {{"is infatuated!" = [**+**](`#?menudm|infatuationstart)}} {{"can they act?" = [**+**](`#?menudm|infatuationsave)}}

Dodging
Once per battle a trainer can dodge any attack about to hit them. After the accuracy roll has succeeded and damage is rolled, a Trainer can decide to Dodge an attack, completely negating its effects. If the trainer was unaware of the attacker they can only reduce the damage by half and still suffer any other effects of the attack.
At level 6 a trainer can dodge twice per battle.
Once a trainer has multiple uses of dodge they can choose to use two of their dodges to completely negate the effects of an attack they were not aware of.

Intercepting
As a reaction a trainer can command a Pok√©mon within reach of a melee attacker and its target to intercept an attack. The Pok√©mon intercepting the attack becomes the new target and suffers the effects of being hit by that attack.
A Pok√©mon can intercept a ranged attack in the same manner but does not need to be within reach of the attacker and target. Instead, the interceptor of a ranged attack must be within reach of the path the ranged attack must travel to hit the target.
To intercept an attack the trainer and Pok√©mon must be aware of the attacker. A Pok√©mon cannot evade an attack they are intercepting.

rush
This move requires a Pok√©mon to move freely during the attack. If the Pok√©mon is immobilized due to cords, ropes, physical restraints, or a grapple they can make a STR check as part of this move to attempt to break free. The DC of this STR check is based on the object or an opposed STR check by the Pok√©mon that immobilized the user. If the user fails the STR check, they do not break free and the move fails."

escape
You attempt to escape from a successful grapple (see Grapple). Make an opposed save of your Body or Reflex against the Body of your opponent. If you succeed, you end the grapple and can move up to half your normal speed. If you fail, you are still grappled.
Pok√©mon that are insubstantial, slimy, or otherwise difficult to hold gain +3 to escaping a grapple.
Any Pok√©mon that can become incorporeal may escape a grapple automatically any time they do so.

knockback
"A move with knockback will move the target a number of squares equal to the user's (STR + X) - (the targets STR). X is a value set by the move."
"If the target has a fly speed they can use the Acrobatics skill to reduce the damage (from a knockback) by 1d10 per degree of success above DC 15."

grapple
You attempt to enter a grapple by grabbing and holding a target. Make an opposed Body check against their Reflex or Body save. If you win with one degree of success, the target loses their evasion bonus and cannot move. Two or more degrees you trap your target (if it‚Äôs a Pok√©mon it cannot be recalled) and they cannot make physical attacks. You lose your evasion bonus while grappling an opponent. You can maintain a successful grapple as a free action each turn, but cannot perform other actions requiring the use of your grappling  limb(s) while doing so. You can drag a grappled target along with you when you move. The target gets a Strength resistance check against your Strength. If it fails, you move and the target moves along with you. If the target resists, you are immobilized that turn unless you release your hold on the target. You can end a grapple (releasing your target) as a free action. If you are unable to take the free action to maintain the hold, the target is automatically released. A target can attempt to escape from a grapple as part of a move action (see Escape).
The Pok√©mon moves Bind, Clamp, and Wrap enter a grapple with an AC of 3 (Likely easier than an opposed check). If a Pok√©mon has the move Bind, Clamp, or Wrap, they gain a passive +3 to checks to maintain a grapple. The damage for Bind, Clamp, and Wrap automatically occur every turn a grapple is maintained, if the grappler so desires.
Pok√©mon with long bodies, extra arms, or any other reasonable advantage gain +3 to maintaining a grapple.

Falling
A fall inflicts 1d6 damage per square fallen, to a maximum of 20d6 damage. Characters with the Acrobatics skill can fall greater distances without risk of damage. Falling into or onto a dangerous surface may cause additional damage, at the PM‚Äôs discretion. Catching a falling person or object requires an Agility check (DC 5). If you successfully catch a falling object, subtract your Strength from the number of falling damage die. Both you and the object divide any remaining damage between you. So if a character with Strength 2 catches someone falling for 8d6 damage, subtract 2 from 8, and both characters take 3d6 damage.

Degrees of Success
Occasionally a skill or other check will have varying levels of success. In this case, the check will state that for every degree of success a certain outcome will result. One degree of success is passing the base DC, and for every 5 above the DC of the check result another degree of success occurs.

flinch
priority 
cover

knockback
"A move with knockback will move the target a number of squares equal to the user's (STR + X) - (the targets STR). X is a value set by the move."
"If the target has a fly speed they can use the Acrobatics skill to reduce the damage (from a knockback) by 1d10 per degree of success above DC 15."

rush
This move requires a Pok√©mon to move freely during the attack. If the Pok√©mon is immobilized due to cords, ropes, physical restraints, or a grapple they can make a STR check as part of this move to attempt to break free. The DC of this STR check is based on the object or an opposed STR check by the Pok√©mon that immobilized the user. If the user fails the STR check, they do not break free and the move fails."

Saving Throws
Many circumstances call for what is termed a ‚ÄúSaving Throw.‚Äù Saving throws are used to overcome, resist, or dodge various effects in the world, such a poisons, fear-effects, or falling rocks. When asked to make a saving throw, roll a d20, similar to making a skill check, but instead add the relevant bonus to whatever type of save is being made. The bonus a character has to each save is calculated based on their attributes (or STATs for Pok√©mon), as detailed in the Creation chapter (pg. 4).

Falling
A fall inflicts 1d6 damage per square fallen, to a maximum of 20d6 damage. Characters with the Acrobatics skill can fall greater distances without risk of damage. Falling into or onto a dangerous surface may cause additional damage, at the PM‚Äôs discretion. Catching a falling person or object requires an Agility check (DC 5). If you successfully catch a falling object, subtract your Strength from the number of falling damage die. Both you and the object divide any remaining damage between you. So if a character with Strength 2 catches someone falling for 8d6 damage, subtract 2 from 8, and both characters take 3d6 damage.

SKILLS SUMMARY
Your character‚Äôs skills represent a variety of abilities, and you get better at them as you advance in level. A skill check takes into account your training (trained skill bonus), natural talent (attribute score), experience (trainer level), and luck (the die roll). This chapter has the details and rules for each skill.
         Skill Basics
To make a skill check, roll:
1d20 + trained skill bonus + key attribute + 1‚ÅÑ2 level + miscellaneous modifiers
A skill check is made just like an accuracy roll or saving throw. The higher the roll, the better. You‚Äôre either trying to get a result that equals or exceeds a certain Difficulty Class (DC), or you‚Äôre trying to beat another character‚Äôs check result. For instance, to sneak quietly past a guard, Joey needs to beat the guard‚Äôs Perception check with a Stealth check.
When adding ‚Äú1‚ÅÑ2 trainer level,‚Äù always round down (a 1st level character adds +0).
The ‚Äúkey attribute‚Äù is the character‚Äôs bonus or penalty for the skill‚Äôs associated attribute (Strength, Agility, Vitality, Spirit, Awareness, and Intelligence). The key attribute for each skill is explained below.
‚ÄúMiscellaneous modifiers‚Äù include penalties for armor or poor circumstances and bonuses from traits and good circumstances.
Some skills cannot be used unless the trainer is trained in the skill, such as Computers. Other skills, like Persuasion, can be used untrained, but the +5 trained bonus will not apply.
How Skills Work
A character begins play with four trained skills. The trait Skill Training can be taken at any time, and allows for a character to pick two more skills that he or she can be trained in. The skills Mysticism, Psychonesis and Styler require special traits to learn, every other skill can be picked with the starting four skills or the Skill Training trait.
Making Skill Checks
When your character makes a skill check, roll 1d20 and add the trained skill bonus (if trained) + your key attribute + 1‚ÅÑ2 level + misc modifiers. Success in the skill attempt depends on the difficulty of the task at hand.
Example: Joey, a 1st level trainer, has an Awareness of 1 and is trying to find his way out of Viridian forest. First he attempts a Survival check. Joey is trained in Survival, so he gets the +5 trained skill bonus. He rolls 1d20 and adds one-half his level (+0), his Awareness (+1), and his trained skill bonus (+5). He gets a 7 on the d20 roll, and he adds everything together to get a total of 13. Unfortunately, the PM knows that because of the storm blowing through the woods the DC to find his way out is 15. Joey is getting lost! However, the PM also knows that Joey is from Viridian Forest and spent most of his life tromping through those woods. The PM decides that having lived in the area grants a favorable circumstance bonus of +2, for a total of 15, and it turns out that Joey sees a familiar landmark in the distance and gets home before the storm hits.
Advancing Skills
Ùè∞©Ùè∞ÑÙè∞íÙè∞òÙè∞ä Ùè∞ê Ùè∞òÙè∞ÉÙè∞êÙè∞éÙè∞êÙè∞òÙè∞ÇÙè∞äÙè∞éÙè∞ãÙè∞Ö Ùè∞ÖÙè∞ìÙè∞ÑÙè∞ïÙè∞ï Ùè∞áÙè∞àÙè∞åÙè∞ÑÙè∞çÙè∞ÑÙè∞äÙè∞éÙè∞Ö Ùè∞êÙè∞éÙè∞ä Ùè∞õÙè∞êÙè∞ÖÙè∞äÙè∞å on trainer level, they automatically increase as the character gains levels. When a character reaches 2nd level, all of his skill modifiers Ùè∞ü in both trained and untrained skills Ùè∞ü Ùè∞ÑÙè∞íÙè∞òÙè∞éÙè∞äÙè∞êÙè∞ÖÙè∞ä Ùè∞õÙè∞ô Ùè∞ºÙè∞ù Ùè∞™ Ùè∞òÙè∞ÉÙè∞êÙè∞éÙè∞êÙè∞òÙè∞ÇÙè∞äÙè∞éÙè∞ãÙè∞Ö Ùè∞ÖÙè∞ìÙè∞ÑÙè∞ïÙè∞ï modifiers can also be increased by traits.
Degrees of Success
Occasionally a skill or other check will have varying levels of success. In this case, the check will state that for every degree of success a certain outcome will result. One degree of success is passing the base DC, and for every 5 above the DC of the check result another degree of success occurs.
Types of Skill Checks
When you use a skill, you make a skill check to see how well you do. The higher the result on your skill check, the better you do. Based on the circumstances, your result must equal or exceed a particular number (a DC or the result of an opposed skill check) for you to use the skill successfully. The harder the task, the higher the number you need to roll.
Circumstances can affect your check. If your free to work without distractions, you can make a careful attempt and avoid simple mistakes. If you have lots of time, you can try over and over again, assuring that you eventually succeed. If others help you, you may succeed where otherwise you would fail.
Opposed Check
Some skill checks are opposed checks. They are made against a randomized number, Ùè∞ñÙè∞ÖÙè∞ñÙè∞êÙè∞ïÙè∞ïÙè∞ô Ùè∞êÙè∞íÙè∞àÙè∞ÇÙè∞ÉÙè∞äÙè∞é Ùè∞òÙè∞ÉÙè∞êÙè∞éÙè∞êÙè∞òÙè∞ÇÙè∞äÙè∞éÙè∞ãÙè∞Ö Ùè∞ÖÙè∞ìÙè∞ÑÙè∞ïÙè∞ï Ùè∞òÙè∞ÉÙè∞äÙè∞òÙè∞ì Ùè∞éÙè∞äÙè∞ÖÙè∞ñÙè∞ïÙè∞ÇÙè∞ù For example, to sneak up on a guard, you Ùè∞íÙè∞äÙè∞äÙè∞å Ùè∞ÇÙè∞à Ùè∞õÙè∞äÙè∞êÙè∞Ç Ùè∞ÇÙè∞ÉÙè∞ä Ùè∞ëÙè∞ñÙè∞êÙè∞éÙè∞åÙè∞ãÙè∞Ö Ùè∞öÙè∞äÙè∞éÙè∞òÙè∞äÙè∞öÙè∞ÇÙè∞ÑÙè∞àÙè∞í Ùè∞òÙè∞ÉÙè∞äÙè∞òÙè∞ì results with your Stealth check result. You make a Stealth check, and the PM makes a Perception check for the guard. Whoever scores the higher result wins the contest.
For ties on opposed checks, the character with the higher skill modifier wins. If those scores are the same, roll again.
Check Against a Difficulty Class (DC)
Some checks are made against a Difficulty Class (DC). The DC is a number set by the PM (using the skill rules as a guideline) that you must score as a result on your skill check to succeed. For example, climbing the outer wall of a ruined warehouse may have a DC of 15. To climb the wall, you must get a result of 15 or better on an Athletics check.

Concealment
To attack a target, you first have to have some idea of where to aim your attack. If you can perceive something then you can target it with an attack. If you cannot clearly perceive the target, then it has concealment from you.
Partial Concealment applies a ‚Äì3 circumstance penalty to your attack check for not being able to clearly perceive your target. Partial concealment includes conditions like dim lighting, foliage, heavy precipitation, fog, smoke, and the like.
Total Concealment applies a ‚Äì8 circumstance penalty to your attack check for not being able to perceive the target at all, presuming the attacker even knows (or guesses) the right area to target. It includes conditions like total darkness, heavy smoke or fog, attacking an invisible creature, and so forth
Cover
Targets may also hide behind obstructions to gain cover against your attacks. Obstructions that do not physically block attacks but simply make the target harder to perceive‚Äî such as lighting, fog, or foliage‚Äîprovide concealment rather than cover.
Partial Cover applies a +3 circumstance bonus to Evasion. It generally means about half of the target is behind cover, such as around a corner, behind a tree or pillar, or a low wall.
Total Cover applies a +6 circumstance bonus to Evasion, with three-quarters or more of the target behind cover, like a narrow window, or crouched behind a wall.
If a target is completely behind cover, then you cannot attack that target (although you can attack the cover itself).
Cover also grants a circumstance bonus to reflex saves against area effects so long as the target has cover with respect to the origin point of the effect. So someone behind total cover also gains a +6 to reflex checks against area effects.

Save Ends
Some moves inflict penalties, repeating damage, status conditions, or other negative effects. Many of these effects can be ended by the victim making a successful savings throw. The DC for these save throws is equal to 10 + BST of the Pok√©mon who inflicted the effect. The BST added to the DC is Sp.ATK for Special moves or ATK for physical moves. If it is a status move, the user of the move can make the save DC 10+ Sp.ATK or ATK, whichever is higher.





The term grounded is used to describe a Pok√©mon that can be affected by damaging Ground-type moves and several other associated effects.
Ungrounded Pok√©mon
Several characteristics may make a Pok√©mon ungrounded.
A Pok√©mon is ungrounded if any of the following apply (and there is no effect that makes it grounded).
It has the Flying type.
It has the Ability Levitate.
It is holding an Air Balloon.
It is under the effect of Magnet Rise or Telekinesis.
Some of these characteristics can be negated by certain moves or Abilities, such as Gastro Acid or Klutz. Additionally, during the execution of a move that ignores Abilities or an Ability that ignores other Abilities, Levitate is ignored, so Pok√©mon that are only ungrounded due to it are treated as if they were grounded.
Pok√©mon that are in the semi-invulnerable turn of a move (including the target of Sky Drop) are also unaffected by effects that only work against grounded Pok√©mon. However, this status does not make them immune to Ground-type moves per se‚Äîthey can still be affected by Ground-type moves if those moves successfully hit them (via the effects of No Guard, Lock-On, or Mind Reader), and a Pok√©mon using Dig can still be hit by Earthquake, Magnitude and Fissure. Additionally, a Pok√©mon in a semi-invulnerable turn of a move hit by Smack Down or Thousand Arrows will not gain the smacked down status unless it is also ungrounded (but Pok√©mon in the semi-invulnerable turn of Fly or Bounce will still be knocked out of the move).
Grounded Pok√©mon
By default, grounded Pok√©mon are simply those that are not ungrounded. However, there are also several effects that will negate a Pok√©mon's ungrounded status, making it grounded.
A Pok√©mon will be grounded if any of the following apply.
It is holding an Iron Ball.
It is under the effect of Ingrain (Generation IV onward) or Smack Down/Thousand Arrows.
Gravity is in effect.
The move Roost removes the user's Flying type for one turn; while it does not directly make the user grounded, if the user is only ungrounded due to being Flying type, it will remain ungrounded until it regains its Flying type at the end of that turn.
Inverse Battles and the Ring Target can make Flying-type Pok√©mon able to be affected by damaging Ground-type moves, but they do not cause the Pok√©mon to become grounded; all other relevant effects still consider the Pok√©mon to be ungrounded.
Effects of grounded status
Pok√©mon that are ungrounded are immune to all damaging Ground-type moves, except Thousand Arrows.
Ungrounded Pok√©mon are also immune to:
the entry hazards Spikes, Toxic Spikes, and Sticky Web.
the move Rototiller.
the effects of terrain.
the Ability Arena Trap.
If a grounded Poison-type Pok√©mon is sent out while Toxic Spikes are on its side of the field, Toxic Spikes will be removed.

Concealment
To attack a target, you first have to have some idea of where to aim your attack. If you can perceive something then you can target it with an attack. If you cannot clearly perceive the target, then it has concealment from you.
Partial Concealment applies a ‚Äì3 circumstance penalty to your attack check for not being able to clearly perceive your target. Partial concealment includes conditions like dim lighting, foliage, heavy precipitation, fog, smoke, and the like.
Total Concealment applies a ‚Äì8 circumstance penalty to your attack check for not being able to perceive the target at all, presuming the attacker even knows (or guesses) the right area to target. It includes conditions like total darkness, heavy smoke or fog, attacking an invisible creature, and so forth
Cover
Targets may also hide behind obstructions to gain cover against your attacks.
Obstructions that do not physically block attacks but simply make the target harder to perceive‚Äî such as lighting, fog, or foliage‚Äîprovide concealment rather than cover.
Partial Cover applies a +3 circumstance bonus to Evasion. It generally means about half of the target is behind cover, such as around a corner, behind a tree or pillar, or a low wall.

%{ROLL|dmg_flat_fall_notype}
A fall inflicts 1d6 damage per square fallen, to a maximum of 20d6 damage. Characters with the Acrobatics skill can fall greater distances without risk of damage. Falling into or onto a dangerous surface may cause additional damage, at the GM‚Äôs discretion. Catching a falling person or object requires an Agility check (DC 5). If you successfully catch a falling object, subtract your Strength from the number of falling damage die. Both you and the object divide any remaining damage between you. So if a character with Strength 2 catches someone falling for 8d6 damage, subtract 2 from 8, and both characters take 3d6 damage. ???

%{VALUE|template_roll} {{name=}} {{Action = Intercept}}
allyswitch
%{VALUE|template_moves} {{name=Ally Switch}} {{Type = PSYCHIC, Status}} {{Range = 10, Interrupt}} {{ACC = N/A}} {{Effect = The user switches places with an ally within range. If the ally was being targeted by an attack the user becomes the new target for that attack.
craftyshield
%{VALUE|template_moves} {{name=Crafty Shield}} {{Type = FAIRY, Status}} {{Range = 6, Interrupt}} {{ACC = N/A}} {{Effect = The user intercepts a status attack for its allies. Crafty Shield may be used from 6 squares away from the attack path. Crafty shield allows the user to intercept for up to 3 allies as long as they are with range. The user and protected allies suffer no effects of the attack. Available 1/Battle.
matblock
%{VALUE|template_moves} {{name=Mat Block}} {{Type = FIGHTING, Status}} {{Range = Burst 1}} {{ACC = N/A}} {{Effect = If the user intercepts an attack for an ally Mat Block may be used as a free action to allow the user to intercept the attack for all allies in range. The user and protected allies suffer no effects of the attack. You may only use Mat Block during the first round the user is deployed (redeploying allows another use of Mat Block). Available Daily.
quickguard
%{VALUE|template_moves} {{name=Quick Guard}} {{Type = FIGHTING, Status}} {{Range = Interrupt}} {{ACC = N/A}} {{Effect = If the user intercepts a priority attack for an ally Quick Guard may be used as an interrupt to allow the user to intercept the attack for an additional ally. The additional ally must be adjacent to the first. The user and protected allies suffer no effects of the attack. Available 1/Battle.
wideguard
%{VALUE|template_moves} {{name=Wide Guard}} {{Type = ROCK, Status}} {{Range = Interrupt}} {{ACC = N/A}} {{Effect = If the user intercepts an attack for an ally Wide Guard may be used as an interrupt to allow the user to intercept the attack for an additional ally. The additional ally must be adjacent to the first. The user and protected allies suffer no effects of the attack. Available 1/Battle.}
Intercepting
As a reaction a trainer can command a Pok√©mon within reach of a melee attacker and its target to intercept an attack. The Pok√©mon intercepting the attack becomes the new target and suffers the effects of being hit by that attack.
A Pok√©mon can intercept a ranged attack in the same manner but does not need to be within reach of the attacker and target. Instead, the interceptor of a ranged attack must be within reach of the path the ranged attack must travel to hit the target.
To intercept an attack the trainer and Pok√©mon must be aware of the attacker. A Pok√©mon cannot evade an attack they are intercepting.

%{ROLL|use_action_snatch}
???

18, /w in character sheet, under abilities, change `%{MOVE|hiddenpower} to `%{MOVE|hiddenpower_water} }
-------
([[0@{selected|HIDDEN-POWER}]]-abs([[0@{selected|HIDDEN-POWER}]]-1))={ 1  -1 }
{ 1  -1 } - 1 = { 0 , -2 }
{ 0 , -2 } * 3 = { 0 , -6 }
abs({ 0 , -6 }) + [[0@{selected|HIDDEN-POWER}]] = { itself , 6 }
=
[[abs((([[0@{selected|HIDDEN-POWER}]]-abs([[0@{selected|HIDDEN-POWER}]]-1))-1)*3)+[[0@{selected|HIDDEN-POWER}]]]]
(how to disregard above 18 and below 0?)
[[{floor({ceil([[0@{selected|HIDDEN-POWER}]])+%{VALUE|safetyroll},18+%{VALUE|safetyroll}}kl1),0+%{VALUE|safetyroll}}kh1]]
this just rounds down/up to 18/0 actually
but turn out-of-range into 0?
{ceil([[0@{selected|HIDDEN-POWER}]])+%{VALUE|safetyroll},18+%{VALUE|safetyroll}}kh1
x = { 0 , itself }

%{ROLL|use_move_painsplit}
???
The current HP of the user and the target are added together then split in half. Both the user and the target have their HP set to this value (but not above their max). This attack cannot miss. Available 2/Day.}}

%{ROLL|use_move_payday}
???
The user creates actual, valuable coins with this move that are shot through the area. The value of the coins is equal to the level of the user *20.
&{template:default} {{name=AOE Roll}} {{ACC = 1d20 + 2 + #attackmod = [[ 1d20#crit20 + 2 + #attackmod ]]}} {{DMG = 2d8 + #attack + #stab|NORMAL = [[ 2d8 + #attack + #stab|NORMAL ]]}} {{= #name creates coins worth [[%{VALUE|level}*20]] Pokedollars!}} {{ vs = [**+**](`#damage|physical|NORMAL)}}

%{ROLL|use_move_psychoshift}
???
The user removes all status conditions from itself and inflicts them on the target.
